Vice versa case also applies.\\n291: func (p *XdsProxy) StreamAggregatedResources(downstream DiscoveryStream) error {\\n292: \\tproxyLog.Debugf(\\\"accepted XDS connection from Envoy, forwarding to upstream XDS server\\\")\\n293: \\treturn p.handleStream(downstream)\\n294: }\\n295: \\n296: func (p *XdsProxy) handleStream(downstream adsStream) error {\\n297: \\tcon := &ProxyConnection{\\n298: \\t\\tconID:           connectionNumber.Inc(),\\n299: \\t\\tupstreamError:   make(chan error), // can be produced by recv and send\\n300: \\t\\tdownstreamError: make(chan error), // can be produced by recv and send\\n301: \\t\\t// Requests channel is unbounded. The Envoy<->XDS Proxy<->Istiod system produces a natural\\n302: \\t\\t// looping of Recv and Send. Due to backpressure introduced by gRPC natively (that is, Send() can\\n303: \\t\\t// only send so much data without being Recv'd before it starts blocking), along with the\\n304: \\t\\t// backpressure provided by our channels, we have a risk of deadlock where both Xdsproxy and\\n305: \\t\\t// Istiod are trying to Send, but both are blocked by gRPC backpressure until Recv() is called.\\n306: \\t\\t// However, Recv can fail to be called by Send being blocked. This can be triggered by the two\\n307: \\t\\t// sources in our system (Envoy request and Istiod pushes) producing more events than we can keep\\n308: \\t\\t// up with.\\n309: \\t\\t// See https://github.com/istio/istio/issues/39209 for more information\\n310: \\t\\t//\\n311: \\t\\t// To prevent these issues, we need to either:\\n312: \\t\\t// 1. Apply backpressure directly to Envoy requests or Istiod pushes\\n313: \\t\\t// 2. Make part of the system unbounded\\n314: \\t\\t//\\n315: \\t\\t// (1) is challenging because we cannot do a conditional Recv (for Envoy requests), and changing\\n316: \\t\\t// the control plane requires substantial changes. Instead, we make the requests channel\\n317: \\t\\t// unbounded. This is the least likely to cause issues as the messages we store here are the\\n318: \\t\\t// smallest relative to other channels.\\n319: \\t\\trequestsChan: channels.NewUnbounded[*discovery.DiscoveryRequest](),\\n320: \\t\\t// Allow a buffer of 1. Vice versa case also applies.\\n291: func (p *XdsProxy) StreamAggregatedResources(downstream DiscoveryStream) error {\\n292: \\tproxyLog.Debugf(\\\"accepted XDS connection from Envoy, forwarding to upstream XDS server\\\")\\n293: \\treturn p.handleStream(downstream)\\n294: }\\n295: \\n296: func (p *XdsProxy) handleStream(downstream adsStream) error {\\n297: \\tcon := &ProxyConnection{\\n298: \\t\\tconID:           connectionNumber.Inc(),\\n299: \\t\\tupstreamError:   make(chan error), // can be produced by recv and send\\n300: \\t\\tdownstreamError: make(chan error), // can be produced by recv and send\\n301: \\t\\t// Requests channel is unbounded. The Envoy<->XDS Proxy<->Istiod system produces a natural\\n302: \\t\\t// looping of Recv and Send. Due to backpressure introduced by gRPC natively (that is, Send() can\\n303: \\t\\t// only send so much data without being Recv'd before it starts blocking), along with the\\n304: \\t\\t// backpressure provided by our channels, we have a risk of deadlock where both Xdsproxy and\\n305: \\t\\t// Istiod are trying to Send, but both are blocked by gRPC backpressure until Recv() is called.\\n306: \\t\\t// However, Recv can fail to be called by Send being blocked. This can be triggered by the two\\n307: \\t\\t// sources in our system (Envoy request and Istiod pushes) producing more events than we can keep\\n308: \\t\\t// up with.\\n309: \\t\\t// See https://github.com/istio/istio/issues/39209 for more information\\n310: \\t\\t//\\n311: \\t\\t// To prevent these issues, we need to either:\\n312: \\t\\t// 1. Apply backpressure directly to Envoy requests or Istiod pushes\\n313: \\t\\t// 2. Make part of the system unbounded\\n314: \\t\\t//\\n315: \\t\\t// (1) is challenging because we cannot do a conditional Recv (for Envoy requests), and changing\\n316: \\t\\t// the control plane requires substantial changes. Instead, we make the requests channel\\n317: \\t\\t// unbounded. This is the least likely to cause issues as the messages we store here are the\\n318: \\t\\t// smallest relative to other channels.\\n319: \\t\\trequestsChan: channels.NewUnbounded[*discovery.DiscoveryRequest](),\\n320: \\t\\t// Allow a buffer of 1. Vice versa case also applies.\n291: func (p *XdsProxy) StreamAggregatedResources(downstream DiscoveryStream) error {\n292: \tproxyLog.Debugf(\"accepted XDS connection from Envoy, forwarding to upstream XDS server\")\n293: \treturn p.handleStream(downstream)\n294: }\n295: \n296: func (p *XdsProxy) handleStream(downstream adsStream) error {\n297: \tcon := &ProxyConnection{\n298: \t\tconID:           connectionNumber.Inc(),\n299: \t\tupstreamError:   make(chan error), // can be produced by recv and send\n300: \t\tdownstreamError: make(chan error), // can be produced by recv and send\n301: \t\t// Requests channel is unbounded. The Envoy<->XDS Proxy<->Istiod system produces a natural\n302: \t\t// looping of Recv and Send. Due to backpressure introduced by gRPC natively (that is, Send() can\n303: \t\t// only send so much data without being Recv'd before it starts blocking), along with the\n304: \t\t// backpressure provided by our channels, we have a risk of deadlock where both Xdsproxy and\n305: \t\t// Istiod are trying to Send, but both are blocked by gRPC backpressure until Recv() is called.\n306: \t\t// However, Recv can fail to be called by Send being blocked. This can be triggered by the two\n307: \t\t// sources in our system (Envoy request and Istiod pushes) producing more events than we can keep\n308: \t\t// up with.\n309: \t\t// See https://github.com/istio/istio/issues/39209 for more information\n310: \t\t//\n311: \t\t// To prevent these issues, we need to either:\n312: \t\t// 1. Apply backpressure directly to Envoy requests or Istiod pushes\n313: \t\t// 2. Make part of the system unbounded\n314: \t\t//\n315: \t\t// (1) is challenging because we cannot do a conditional Recv (for Envoy requests), and changing\n316: \t\t// the control plane requires substantial changes. Instead, we make the requests channel\n317: \t\t// unbounded. This is the least likely to cause issues as the messages we store here are the\n318: \t\t// smallest relative to other channels.\n319: \t\trequestsChan: channels.NewUnbounded[*discovery.DiscoveryRequest](),\n320: \t\t// Allow a buffer of 1. During\\n191: \\t\\t// loading request, concurrency=1. Original code avoided the mutexes by doing both 'push' and 'process requests' in same thread.\n139: func (s *DiscoveryServer) processRequest(req *discovery.DiscoveryRequest, con *Connection) error {\n140: \tstype := v3.GetShortType(req.TypeUrl)\n141: \tlog.Debugf(\"ADS:%s: REQ %s resources:%d nonce:%s version:%s \", stype,\n142: \t\tcon.ID(), len(req.ResourceNames), req.ResponseNonce, req.VersionInfo)\n143: \tif req.TypeUrl == v3.HealthInfoType {\n144: \t\ts.handleWorkloadHealthcheck(con.proxy, req)\n145: \t\treturn nil\n146: \t}\n147: \n148: \t// For now, don't let xDS piggyback debug requests start watchers.\n149: \tif strings.HasPrefix(req.TypeUrl, v3.DebugType) {\n150: \t\treturn s.pushXds(con,\n151: \t\t\t&model.WatchedResource{TypeUrl: req.TypeUrl, ResourceNames: sets.New(req.ResourceNames...)},\n152: \t\t\t&model.PushRequest{Full: true, Push: con.proxy.LastPushContext, Forced: true})\n153: \t}\n154: \n155: \tshouldRespond, delta := xds.ShouldRespond(con.proxy, con.ID(), req)\n156: \tif !shouldRespond {\n157: \t\treturn nil\n158: \t}\n159: \n160: \trequest := &model.PushRequest{\n161: \t\tFull:   true,\n162: \t\tPush:   con.proxy.LastPushContext,\n163: \t\tReason: model.NewReasonStats(model.ProxyRequest),\n164: \n165: \t\t// The usage of LastPushTime (rather than time.Now()), is critical here for correctness; This time\n166: \t\t// is used by the XDS cache to determine if a entry is stale. During\n191: \t\t// loading request, concurrency=1. Once that request is done, concurrency is enabled.\n192: \t\t// However, the XDS stream is long lived, so the first request would block all others. As a\n193: \t\t// result, we should exit the first request immediately; clients will retry.\n194: \t\tfirstRequest.Store(false)\n195: \t\treturn status.Error(codes.Unavailable, \"server warmup not complete; try again\")\n196: \t}\n197: \t// Check if server is ready to accept clients and process new requests.\n198: \t// Currently ready means caches have been synced and hence can build\n199: \t// clusters correctly. Without this check, InitContext() call below would\n200: \t// initialize with empty config, leading to reconnected Envoys losing\n201: \t// configuration. This is an additional safety check inaddition to adding\n202: \t// cachesSynced logic to readiness probe to handle cases where kube-proxy\n203: \t// ip tables update latencies.\n204: \t// See https://github.com/istio/istio/issues/25495.\n205: \tif !s.IsServerReady() {\n206: \t\treturn status.Error(codes.Unavailable, \"server is not ready to serve discovery information\")\n207: \t}\n208: \n209: \tctx := stream.Context()\n210: \tpeerAddr := \"0.0.0.0\"\n211: \tif peerInfo, ok := peer.FromContext(ctx);
